    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

<span id="freeTextContainer12278503281443366278">Tommy Beresford and Prudence 'Tuppence' Cowley are young, in love… and flat broke. Just after Great War, there are few jobs available and the couple are desperately short of money. Restless for excitement, they decide to embark on a daring business scheme: Young Adventurers Ltd.—"willing to do anything, go anywhere." Hiring themselves out proves to be a smart move for the </span>
  <span id="freeText12278503281443366278" style="display:none">Tommy Beresford and Prudence 'Tuppence' Cowley are young, in love… and flat broke. Just after Great War, there are few jobs available and the couple are desperately short of money. Restless for excitement, they decide to embark on a daring business scheme: Young Adventurers Ltd.—"willing to do anything, go anywhere." Hiring themselves out proves to be a smart move for the couple. In their first assignment for the mysterious Mr. Whittingtont, all Tuppence has to do in their first job is take an all-expense paid trip to Paris and pose as an American named Jane Finn. But with the assignment comes a bribe to keep quiet, a threat to her life, and the disappearance of her new employer. Now their newest job are playing detective.<br /><br />Where is the real Jane Finn? The mere mention of her name produces a very strange reaction all over London. So strange, in fact, that they decided to find this mysterious missing lady. She has been missing for five years. And neither her body nor the secret documents she was carrying have ever been found. Now post-war England's economic recovery depends on finding her and getting the papers back. But he two young working undercover for the British ministry know only that her name and the only photo of her is in the hands of her rich American cousin. It isn’t long before they find themselves plunged into more danger than they ever could have imagined—a danger that could put an abrupt end to their business… and their lives.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12278503281443366278" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_2302589775" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2302589775" />
    <a title="Anne" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1720620-anne"><img alt="Anne" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1415374035p2/1720620.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2302589775?book_show_action=true">Mar 07, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Anne" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Anne" href="/user/show/1720620-anne">Anne</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1720620-anne?shelf=agatha-christie">agatha-christie</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1720620-anne?shelf=kindle">kindle</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1720620-anne?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2302589775" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15685501851685639066"><b>Secret Adversary</b> is the first Tommy & Tuppence novel. <br/><i>Ta-da!</i><br/><br/> <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1520459407i/25178010._SX540_.jpg' width='400' height='270' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/> <br/>I'm not going to claim that it's <i>great</i>, but it was entertaining. And Christie managed to make me think I <b>
  <i>KNEW</i>
</b> who the hell dunnit, only to jerk the rug out from underneath me...again. <--to be fair, that's kind of her thing, you know?<br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1520459683i/25178026._SX540_.jpg' width='400' height='220' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>You know what was cute, though? All the <i>snappy</i> dialogue between the not-quite-yet lovebirds. I mean, it's probably not snappy by today's standards, but back in the day, I'm betting this was quite the </span>
  <span id="freeText15685501851685639066" style="display:none"><b>Secret Adversary</b> is the first Tommy &amp; Tuppence novel. <br><i>Ta-da!</i><br><br> <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1520459407i/25178010._SX540_.jpg" width="400" height="270" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br> <br>I'm not going to claim that it's <i>great</i>, but it was entertaining. And Christie managed to make me think I <b>
  <i>KNEW</i>
</b> who the hell dunnit, only to jerk the rug out from underneath me...again. &lt;--to be fair, that's kind of her thing, you know?<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1520459683i/25178026._SX540_.jpg" width="400" height="220" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>You know what was cute, though? All the <i>snappy</i> dialogue between the not-quite-yet lovebirds. I mean, it's probably not snappy by today's standards, but back in the day, I'm betting this was quite the sassy back and forth.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1520460434i/25178074._SY540_.jpg" width="400" height="500" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The story is sort of out there with the wacky <i>let's hire these two young people with ZERO experience to save the government from falling into the hands of EEEEEEEVIL men</i> premise, but the characters are adorable. <br>I'll definitely read more of their adventures someday.<br><br><b>PS - Inspector Japp gets a cameo mention in this!</b></span>

<div id="review_1721690586" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1721690586" />
    <a title="James" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7365405-james"><img alt="James" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1522094190p2/7365405.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1721690586?book_show_action=true">Aug 07, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="James" class="user" itemprop="url" name="James" href="/user/show/7365405-james">James</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/33843507-the-secret-adversary">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7365405-james?shelf=3-multi-book-series">3-multi-book-series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7365405-james?shelf=2-fic-cozy-mystery">2-fic-cozy-mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7365405-james?shelf=1-fiction">1-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7365405-james?shelf=9-read-2018-04-april">9-read-2018-04-april</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1721690586" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5020840826224330348">I am hosting an <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/123715.Agatha_Christie' title='Agatha Christie' rel='nofollow noopener'>Agatha Christie</a> Readathon on <a href='https://thisismytruthnow.com/agatha-christie-readathon/' rel='nofollow noopener'>my blog</a> in April 2018 where we are reading one of her books each week. The first book up, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/49596.The_Secret_Adversary__Tommy_and_Tuppence__1_' title='The Secret Adversary (Tommy and Tuppence #1) by Agatha Christie' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Secret Adversary</a>, is the initial entry in the Tommy & Tuppence cozy mystery series she's written. Although I've read a bunch of her novels, I hadn't read anything in this particular series, so I was glad that one of them won the poll to choose our books that I had set up earlier this year.<br/><br/>In this caper, Tommy and Tuppence, ~22 year old somewhat poor residents</span>
  <span id="freeText5020840826224330348" style="display:none">I am hosting an <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/123715.Agatha_Christie" title="Agatha Christie" rel="nofollow noopener">Agatha Christie</a> Readathon on <a href="https://thisismytruthnow.com/agatha-christie-readathon/" rel="nofollow noopener">my blog</a> in April 2018 where we are reading one of her books each week. The first book up, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/49596.The_Secret_Adversary__Tommy_and_Tuppence__1_" title="The Secret Adversary (Tommy and Tuppence #1) by Agatha Christie" rel="nofollow noopener">The Secret Adversary</a>, is the initial entry in the Tommy &amp; Tuppence cozy mystery series she's written. Although I've read a bunch of her novels, I hadn't read anything in this particular series, so I was glad that one of them won the poll to choose our books that I had set up earlier this year.<br /><br />In this caper, Tommy and Tuppence, ~22 year old somewhat poor residents of London around 1920, are bored enough to form a partnership where they will agree to do anything legal to obtain a salary. Tuppence wants to marry rich. Tommy doesn't care. You kinda know they have to end up together, right? A mysterious man overhears their conversation and asks them for help in finding Jane Finn who disappeared when the Lusitania sank nearly five years earlier. She was given a very important government paper by a pseudo-spy who died in the tragedy, but Jane seems to have lost her memory. No one can find her, but there are several ne'er-to-do-wells and government spies searching for her. Though WW1 is over now, if anyone finds out what was written in the papers, it might just ignite another battle. Tommy &amp; Tuppence take the case, but soon find themselves baffled by all the different stories they hear. When they separate to get more done, each is kidnapped and nearly killed for knowing nothing but really knowing something. Then Jane's American cousin helps with the search and leads are finally flooding in around them. Now the little sleuthing pair are on their own and unable to determine who's telling the truth. Think you can? I actually solved this one. <br /><br />Christie is remarkable when it comes to creating suspense, intrigue, and drama in her books. Although the story started off a tad peculiar to me, I slowly became fascinated by how different things were nearly 100 years ago. Between the phrases used to describe people, the quick allegiance people swore to one another, and the methods for doing research, it was outstanding. Sometimes I laughed at their silly tactics, others I thought they made no sense. But it was a different time and place, and under those contexts, it actually made perfect sense. <br /><br />Tommy &amp; Tuppence themselves are also weird. They speak in terms of puzzles, but seem to understand one another. They wish for things they don't need but join forces in a venture that initially makes no sense. I was worried... even thought... did I make a mistake giving this book a chance? But I knew how much people adored them, so I pushed forward and by about 20% in, the book takes on a much more standard mystery and suspense tone.<br /><br />The ending was very well written. The plot is thorough but leaves a lot to the imagination. Do we really ever find out what's written in the government documents? Do we know exactly who kidnapped each of the sleuths? Do we know whether every character was purely good or evil? Not really... there is a bit of vagueness going on, but it doesn't hurt the story. Readers will more than likely fall in love with the duo, get caught up in determining which is the true bad guy, and grow puzzled in trying to decide which information to trust and which information is just a red herring.<br /><br />It's fun to read these capers. It's less about the language and more about the approach to solving a crime. So sit back and relax... let the author dazzle you with her story... and let go of the normal constructs you expect in a mystery novel. I'm going with 4 stars on this one, as I'd more than recommend it, but there were some things I felt could have been handled better. That said... I look forward to reading more in the Tommy &amp; Tuppence series, but that will have to wait. Next week's book is from the Hercule Poirot collection. Join us if you can!</span>
  <a data-text-id="5020840826224330348" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1932802809" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1932802809" />
    <a title="BrokenTune" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10592271-brokentune"><img alt="BrokenTune" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1391017756p2/10592271.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1932802809?book_show_action=true">Mar 05, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="BrokenTune" class="user" itemprop="url" name="BrokenTune" href="/user/show/10592271-brokentune">BrokenTune</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10592271-brokentune?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1932802809" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2703249198693481951"><i>IT was 2 p.m. on the afternoon of May 7, 1915. The Lusitania had been struck by two torpedoes in succession and was sinking rapidly, while the boats were being launched with all possible speed.<br/></i><br/>This is still one of the most intriguing Agatha Christie opening lines I have read (another can be found in Murder on the Orient Express, but I'll get to that in a different post). <br/> <br/>The Secret Adversary is the first adventure of Miss Prudence Cowley and Lieutenant Thomas Beresford, a.k.a. Tommy and Tuppenc</span>
  <span id="freeText2703249198693481951" style="display:none"><i>IT was 2 p.m. on the afternoon of May 7, 1915. The Lusitania had been struck by two torpedoes in succession and was sinking rapidly, while the boats were being launched with all possible speed.<br /></i><br />This is still one of the most intriguing Agatha Christie opening lines I have read (another can be found in Murder on the Orient Express, but I'll get to that in a different post). <br /> <br />The Secret Adversary is the first adventure of Miss Prudence Cowley and Lieutenant Thomas Beresford, a.k.a. Tommy and Tuppence. <br />Tommy and Tuppence have known each other since childhood but lost touch over the years with the exception that they met again in 1916, when Tommy was injured in the war and Tuppence worked as an auxiliary nurse. The story sets in as they meet again for the first time since 1916, now in London in 1920. Both are best described as Bright Young Things of their time, both are broke, and both are looking for way to make some money.<br /> <br />I absolutely love the start of this story, the setting and the dialogue between Tommy and Tuppence. It's fresh, it's witty, it's believable.<br />Christie shines through in every aspect of Tuppence, and, based on descriptions of her own circumstances in Christie's autobiography, I have a hunch that Tommy was somewhat inspired by Christie's then husband Archie.<br /> <br />When thinking about bright young things, I usually first think of Waugh's Vile Bodies. However, what is striking about The Secret Adversary is that it was published in 1922 - a whole 8 years before Vile Bodies!<br /> <br />This is only Christie's 2nd(!) published novel, and yet we get such fun dialogue as this:<br /><i><br />"Rot!" said Tommy hastily. "Well, that's my position. I'm just about desperate."<br />"So am I! I've hung out as long as I could. I've touted round. I've answered advertisements. I've tried every mortal blessed thing. I've screwed and saved and pinched! But it's no good. I shall have to go home!"<br />"Don't you want to?"<br />"Of course I don't want to! What's the good of being sentimental? Father's a dear--I'm awfully fond of him--but you've no idea how I worry him! He has that delightful early Victorian view that short skirts and smoking are immoral. You can imagine what a thorn in the flesh I am to him! He just heaved a sigh of relief when the war took me off. You see, there are seven of us at home. It's awful! All housework and mothers' meetings! I have always been the changeling. I don't want to go back, but--oh, Tommy, what else is there to do?"<br />Tommy shook his head sadly. There was a silence, and then Tuppence burst out: "Money, money, money! I think about money morning, noon and night! I dare say it's mercenary of me, but there it is!"<br />"Same here," agreed Tommy with feeling. <br /></i><br />While I love Tummy and Tuppence, the plot of the story doesn't quite work for me. It's Christie's first attempt at international espionage, and, if you ask me, she should have left it at that. After the two friends discuss an idea to go into business together, the plot snowballs out of control fuelled by the most unlikely of coincidences, and at some point I got confused again (and this was my third re-read!) about who is who and who is bluffing whom. <br /> <br />Mystery-wise, this is not the greatest of stories. However, I'd recommend it just for the sheer fun of getting to know Christie in her early years, before the necessity to make money from writing leads her to develop that famous formula that runs through most of her best known creations.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2703249198693481951" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3460138825" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3460138825" />
    <a title="Sandy *The world could end while I was reading and I would never notice*" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30817744-sandy-the-world-could-end-while-i-was-reading-and-i-would-never-notice"><img alt="Sandy *The world could end while I was reading and I would never notice*" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1509647506p2/30817744.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3460138825?book_show_action=true">Jul 31, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sandy *The world could end while I was reading and I would never notice*" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sandy *The world could end while I was reading and I would never notice*" href="/user/show/30817744-sandy-the-world-could-end-while-i-was-reading-and-i-would-never-notice">Sandy *The world could end while I was reading and I would never notice*</a>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/28203903-the-secret-adversary">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30817744-sandy-the-world-could-end-while-i-was-reading-and-i-would-never-notice?shelf=3-star">3-star</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30817744-sandy-the-world-could-end-while-i-was-reading-and-i-would-never-notice?shelf=2020">2020</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30817744-sandy-the-world-could-end-while-i-was-reading-and-i-would-never-notice?shelf=golden-age-detective-story">golden-age-detective-story</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30817744-sandy-the-world-could-end-while-i-was-reading-and-i-would-never-notice?shelf=crime">crime</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30817744-sandy-the-world-could-end-while-i-was-reading-and-i-would-never-notice?shelf=spy-thriller">spy-thriller</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30817744-sandy-the-world-could-end-while-i-was-reading-and-i-would-never-notice?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30817744-sandy-the-world-could-end-while-i-was-reading-and-i-would-never-notice?shelf=audio">audio</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30817744-sandy-the-world-could-end-while-i-was-reading-and-i-would-never-notice?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3460138825" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1768064942945977837">EXCERPT: It was 2 pm on the afternoon of May 7, 1915. The Lusitania had been struck by two torpedoes in succession and was sinking rapidly, while the boats were being launched with all possible speed. The women and children were being lined up awaiting their turn. Some still clung desperately to husbands and fathers; others clutched their children closely to their breasts. One girl stood alone, slightly apart from the rest. She was quite young, not more than eighteen. She did not seem afraid, an</span>
  <span id="freeText1768064942945977837" style="display:none">EXCERPT: It was 2 pm on the afternoon of May 7, 1915. The Lusitania had been struck by two torpedoes in succession and was sinking rapidly, while the boats were being launched with all possible speed. The women and children were being lined up awaiting their turn. Some still clung desperately to husbands and fathers; others clutched their children closely to their breasts. One girl stood alone, slightly apart from the rest. She was quite young, not more than eighteen. She did not seem afraid, and her grave, steadfast eyes looked straight ahead. <br /><br />'I beg your pardon.'<br /><br />A man's voice beside her made her start and turn. She had noticed the speaker more than once among the first class passengers. There had been a hint of mystery about him which had appealed to her imagination. He spoke to no one. If anyone spoke to him, he was quick to rebuff the overture. Also he had a nervous way of looking over his shoulder with a swift suspicious glance. <br /><br />She noticed now that he was greatly agitated. There were beads of perspiration on his brow. He was evidently in a state of overmastering fear. And yet he did not strike her as the kind of man who would be afraid to meet death!<br /><br />'Yes?' Her grave eyes met his inquiringly. <br /><br />He stood looking at her with a kind of desperate irresolution. <br /><br />'It must be!' He muttered to himself. 'Yes - it is the only way.' Then aloud he said abruptly, 'You are an American?'<br /><br />'Yes.'<br /><br />'A patriotic one?'<br /><br />The girl flushed. <br /><br />'I guess you've no right to ask such a thing! Of course I am!'<br /><br />'Don't be offended. You wouldn't be if you knew how much there was at stake. But I've got to trust someone, and it must be a woman.'<br /><br />'Why?'<br /><br />'Because of 'women and children first'.' He looked round and lowered his voice. 'I'm carrying papers - vitally important papers. They may make all the difference to the allies in the war. You understand? These papers have got to be saved. They've more chance with you than with me. Will you take them?'<br /><br />ABOUT THIS BOOK: Tommy and Tuppence, two young people short of money and restless for excitement, embark on a daring business scheme – Young Adventurers Ltd.<br /><br />Their advertisement says they are ‘willing to do anything, go anywhere’. But their first assignment, for the sinister Mr Whittington, plunges them into more danger than they ever imagined…<br /><br />MY THOUGHTS: Tommy and Tuppence have never been my favourite Christie characters, but I must admit to having quite enjoyed The Secret Adversary, the first in the series, in which we learn about their backgrounds, and how they came to be sleuths. <br /><br />The timeline starts not long before WWII, and then jumps to after the end of the war and the quest to find the young woman to whom the vitally important papers were entrusted. <br /><br />This is rather a good, adventurous romp, and not at all classic Christie. All the same I did quite enjoy trying to figure out just who was the traitor - I was completely wrong! Again. There are Russians, secret meetings with passwords, kidnappings, and murders. <br /><br />While not my favourite Christie, this was still a more enjoyable read than I expected. <br /><br />😊😊😊.3<br /><br />THE AUTHOR: Dame Agatha Mary Clarissa Christie, Lady Mallowan, DBE was an English writer known for her sixty-six detective novels and fourteen short story collections, particularly those revolving around fictional detectives Hercule Poirot and Miss Marple. (Wikipedia)<br /><br />DISCLOSURE: I listened to the audiobook of The Secret Adversary, written by Agatha Christie, narrated by Andrea Giorgani, and published by A.R.N. Publications via Overdrive. All opinions expressed in this review are entirely my own personal opinions. <br /><br />For an explanation of my rating system please refer to my Goodreads.com profile page or the about page on sandysbookaday.wordpress.com <br /><br />This review and others are also published on Twitter, Amazon, Instagram and my webpage <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://sandysbookaday.wordpress.com/2020/08/01/the-secret-adversary-by-agatha-christie/">https://sandysbookaday.wordpress.com/...</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="1768064942945977837" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <a title="Simona B" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5312173-simona-b"><img alt="Simona B" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1408893128p2/5312173.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Simona B" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Simona B" href="/user/show/5312173-simona-b">Simona B</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780007111466" href="/book/show/282900.The_Secret_Adversary">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5312173-simona-b?shelf=1900">1900</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5312173-simona-b?shelf=mystery-and-crime">mystery-and-crime</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5312173-simona-b?shelf=in-italian">in-italian</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1919109105" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1508265005456193788"><b>“Don't be offended because I think you're young. Youth is a failing only too easily outgrown.” </b><br/><br/>I am willing to bet anything that <b>Tommy and Tuppence</b> are the two cutest wannabe detectives in the panorama of <b>spy fiction</b> in its entirety. <br/>Yes, spy fiction: I dove into this expecting a crime story, instead <i>espionage</i> was the key word here. There is no denying that I was a little disappointed and more than a little taken aback, but Christie can do no wrong, even when she <i>does</i> do wrong, so, of course, I </span>
  <span id="freeText1508265005456193788" style="display:none"><b>“Don't be offended because I think you're young. Youth is a failing only too easily outgrown.” </b><br /><br />I am willing to bet anything that <b>Tommy and Tuppence</b> are the two cutest wannabe detectives in the panorama of <b>spy fiction</b> in its entirety. <br />Yes, spy fiction: I dove into this expecting a crime story, instead <i>espionage</i> was the key word here. There is no denying that I was a little disappointed and more than a little taken aback, but Christie can do no wrong, even when she <i>does</i> do wrong, so, of course, I liked it.<br /><br />The plot admittedly works with <b>too many pretty coincidences</b> and happy happenstances, so I wouldn't call it a "serious" espionage novel, and it most certainly won't appeal to fans of that genre. I ended up enjoying it nonetheless because, as I said, the main characters are the most adorable creatures to ever walk the earth, and because Agatha still managed to make up for the naivety of the whole thing with a finale that is, after all, not so predictable.<br /><br /><b>I will obviously read the next novels</b> in the Tommy and Tuppence series, and the collection of short stories too. Plus, (I'm marking it as spoiler, but <i>really now</i>) <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[I'm dying to see them as a married couple <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. I'm sure their banter will be twice as lovely and hilarious.</span>

          </span>

    <a title="Jaya" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/31691644-jaya"><img alt="Jaya" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1584890720p2/31691644.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1666369705?book_show_action=true">Jun 12, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jaya" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jaya" href="/user/show/31691644-jaya">Jaya</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook " href="/book/show/12328636-the-secret-adversary">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31691644-jaya?shelf=bah-humbug">bah-humbug</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31691644-jaya?shelf=shinpi-surir%C4%81-sasupensu-hanzai">shinpi-surirā-sasupensu-hanzai</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31691644-jaya?shelf=kindle">kindle</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31691644-jaya?shelf=mmxvi">mmxvi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31691644-jaya?shelf=buddy-group-read">buddy-group-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31691644-jaya?shelf=re-reads">re-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31691644-jaya?shelf=once-upon-a-time-b4-gr">once-upon-a-time-b4-gr</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31691644-jaya?shelf=did-we-read-the-same-book">did-we-read-the-same-book</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31691644-jaya?shelf=historical">historical</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1666369705" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11358173812737290093">Re read with <i> <b>The Christie Carnage -noobs, middlings & hoity tots </b> </i><br/><br/><b>WARNING</b>: My thoughts are going to be scattered all over this review, <i> Why?</i> Because, I suck at reviewing.<br/><br/><i>Lets begin from the beginning. </i><br/><br/>So, some of the readers at the <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/group/show/729' rel='nofollow noopener'>Indian Readers</a> decided to read the complete works of <i>Agatha Christie</i>. I, being overly curious and enthusiastic, jumped right into with my fellow readers, despite of having read, re-read, watched, heard (audiobooks and those delicious BBC radio plays) multiple number </span>
  <span id="freeText11358173812737290093" style="display:none">Re read with <i> <b>The Christie Carnage -noobs, middlings &amp; hoity tots </b> </i><br /><br /><b>WARNING</b>: My thoughts are going to be scattered all over this review, <i> Why?</i> Because, I suck at reviewing.<br /><br /><i>Lets begin from the beginning. </i><br /><br />So, some of the readers at the <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/group/show/729" rel="nofollow noopener">Indian Readers</a> decided to read the complete works of <i>Agatha Christie</i>. I, being overly curious and enthusiastic, jumped right into with my fellow readers, despite of having read, re-read, watched, heard (audiobooks and those delicious BBC radio plays) multiple number of times. So the book most voted upon (roughly based on chronology of its publishing) was the <i> Secret Adversary </i>, published in the year 1922 (this was after <i>Mysterious Affair at Styles</i>).<br /><br /><i>Disclaimer</i>: Prior to this I had never followed any chronology while reading her works. The primary reason was availability. Whatever books were available in the school and local libraries, had to make do with those. But that was almost 15 years back. (Totally useless information.)<br /><br />Coming back to the book, had I read, <i>The Secret Adversary</i>, some odd 10 years back, this book would have been a winner for me (getting older <s>un</s>fortunately has made me more critical). This book has one of my most favourite tropes- <i> <b>An espionage set during the First World War period</b> </i>. The idea of saving secret documents from the hands of the bad guys during one of my most favourite period of history (should have) got my juices flowing. The story had almost all the elements - secret societies with members having code names, dual identities, chasing and spying sequences, lost memories and of course murder. Despite of the things that should have made this great espionage book, the story went flat for me. <br />The main characters, <i> Tommy</i> &amp; <i>Tuppence </i> (Two people <s>going to extreme lengths </s> trying too hard for the sake of money and some idea of grand adventure) and <i>Julius Hersheimmer </i> somehow seemed a bit caricaturish to me. Exception perhaps was <i> Sir James Peel Edgerton </i> who made a clever and believable character. The plot too, IMO, was a bit too contrived.<br /><br />Then mid way, through the book, I recalled the bad guy was :-/ (curse of re-reading). Was languishing at 50%, had to speed up because my co-readers were already done with it (again completely rambling thoughts)<br /><br />I had started with the intention of giving it at least three stars, chopping off one star now. Was annoyed at times while reading those obvious coincidences and at Tommy’s tomfoolery, the way he would goad his captors.<br />Here's an incident,<br /><br />	<i>"Good morning", said Tommy amiably. "You have NOT used Pear's soap, I see".<br />"No light repartee, have you old bean? There, there, we can't always have brains as well as beauty..."</i><br /><br />Sorry, I was neither amused nor impressed with his bravado.<br /><br />Damn! Thats the reason I don’ t like doing reviews. <br /><br />The Secret Adversary gets only <b>2.25 stars</b> from me.<br /><br />Having said that do not go by my verdict, Goodreads is teeming with good reviews. I would recommend it to all mystery/thriller aficionados</span>
  <a data-text-id="11358173812737290093" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1197737591" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer162233720734880027">2020 Re-read:<br/><br/>This was a very fun re-read. How different it is from Christie's first novel, although it was entertaining to see Inspector Japp show up very briefly during the proceedings. I became aware that Hercules Poirot and Tommy & Tuppence exist in the same environment. <br/><br/>You'd think that I would remember the ending since I only read it two years ago, but no dice. There were plenty of other details that stuck in my mind however. I loved the banter between the main characters and the breakneck </span>
  <span id="freeText162233720734880027" style="display:none">2020 Re-read:<br /><br />This was a very fun re-read. How different it is from Christie's first novel, although it was entertaining to see Inspector Japp show up very briefly during the proceedings. I became aware that Hercules Poirot and Tommy &amp; Tuppence exist in the same environment. <br /><br />You'd think that I would remember the ending since I only read it two years ago, but no dice. There were plenty of other details that stuck in my mind however. I loved the banter between the main characters and the breakneck pace of unlikely events. After all, Tommy and Tuppence are rank amateurs in the spy game, but they turn up more information while flailing around as beginners than the professional spooks have been able to come up with.<br /><br />Highly entertaining. I'll look forward to more adventures of this dynamic duo. My initial rating holds up.<br /><br /><br />ORIGINAL REVIEW:<br /><br /><b>
  <i>***2018 Summer of Spies***</i>
</b><br /><br />I had great fun reading this, the second of Dame Agatha’s books to be published. It is refreshing for its lack of a plot formula, like those developed during her career and well established by books like <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/16307.Hallowe_en_Party__Hercule_Poirot___39_" title="Hallowe'en Party (Hercule Poirot, #39) by Agatha Christie" rel="nofollow noopener">Hallowe'en Party</a>. It is also unusual in its featuring of a couple in the starring roles, Tommy &amp; Tuppence. Plus it incorporates a relatively recent event, the sinking of the Luisitania (1915), <i>The Secret Adversary</i> being published in 1922. I was really struck, however, by the plight of the young people after WWI :<br /><br /><blockquote> "Rot!" said Tommy hastily. "Well, that's my position. I'm just about desperate."<br />"So am I! I've hung out as long as I could. I've touted round. I've answered advertisements. I've tried every mortal blessed thing. I've screwed and saved and pinched! But it's no good. I shall have to go home!"</blockquote><br /><br />Maybe because I live in a town where the economy has been dominated by the (now slumping) petroleum trade for decades and I have also been perusing resumés for a new position in our department. It’s rather sad to see young people bravely putting their best foot forward and knowing that there are much more experienced candidates available. <br /><br />Of course it’s very unrealistic for two young amateurs to fare so well against the Secret Adversary, but it’s more fun than realism would have been. Tuppence, especially, seems to embody the spirit &amp; brains that so many of Christie’s female characters exhibit, giving a hint of what is to come. It was just what I was looking for in a summer read—a rather fluffy &amp; fun adventure.<br /><br />I also liked the author’s dedication: “To all those who lead monotonous lives in the hope that they may experience at second hand the delights and dangers of adventure.” I think she could have dedicated a great many of her books this way.<br /><br />Cross posted at my blog:<br /><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://wanda-thenextfifty.blogspot.com/2020/11/the-secret-adversary-agatha-christie.html">https://wanda-thenextfifty.blogspot.c...</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="162233720734880027" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_41066592" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/41066592" />
    <a title="Laura" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/350677-laura"><img alt="Laura" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1189040780p2/350677.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/41066592?book_show_action=true">Dec 27, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Laura" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Laura" href="/user/show/350677-laura">Laura</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/350677-laura?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/350677-laura?shelf=history">history</a>,

          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer41066592" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16590846990729604778">A short and entertaining read-- entertaining as much for its mystery as for the laughable sensationalism of its topic. Very timely for 1922-- all about bolsheviks and revolutions and Labour Party members and secret treaties, with a hero and heroine full of jolly upper-class Britishness and levity, if not imagination, in tough spots. Very characteristic of an era.<br/><br/>The mystery, though constructed out of sensationalistic and dated elements, has an excellent form. We are told quite frankly in the fir</span>
  <span id="freeText16590846990729604778" style="display:none">A short and entertaining read-- entertaining as much for its mystery as for the laughable sensationalism of its topic. Very timely for 1922-- all about bolsheviks and revolutions and Labour Party members and secret treaties, with a hero and heroine full of jolly upper-class Britishness and levity, if not imagination, in tough spots. Very characteristic of an era.<br /><br />The mystery, though constructed out of sensationalistic and dated elements, has an excellent form. We are told quite frankly in the first few chapters that we will meet the Bad Guy before we know that he IS the Bad Guy-- and then we spend the rest of the book trying to figure out which of the characters he is. Very good, in that regard. Also, as in all good Christie, everyone's got their fingers in the pot somehow-- she manages to keep each character's critical discoveries secret from us until the end-- but even though we're lagging far behind most of the characters, we don't feel stupid because we, as the readers, have our own theories that we don't necessarily want to be spoiled.<br /><br />A very very short one. Read it in an afternoon for a good laugh.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16590846990729604778" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1962874576" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4710364223186614816">Although I've read a huge amount of Agatha Christie stories I've always avoided the four Tommy & Tuppence adventures as they never looked very appealing to me. I have to admit that this, their first adventure, was not as bad as I was expecting. Yes, I did get fed up with the amount of times that they referred to someone as "old bean" & it was a bit light & fluffy for my tastes. <br/>On the other hand the plot zips along quite nicely & there's plenty going on. I really love The Saint stories by Leslie</span>
  <span id="freeText4710364223186614816" style="display:none">Although I've read a huge amount of Agatha Christie stories I've always avoided the four Tommy &amp; Tuppence adventures as they never looked very appealing to me. I have to admit that this, their first adventure, was not as bad as I was expecting. Yes, I did get fed up with the amount of times that they referred to someone as "old bean" &amp; it was a bit light &amp; fluffy for my tastes. <br />On the other hand the plot zips along quite nicely &amp; there's plenty going on. I really love The Saint stories by Leslie Charteris, which began publication at almost the same time as this one. Both are fairly light &amp; easy reads, but somehow the adventures of Simon Templar seem a far better series of yarns to this humble reader.</span>

<div id="review_2830538704" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2830538704" />
    <a title="Juli" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/38617426-juli"><img alt="Juli" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1453642808p2/38617426.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2830538704?book_show_action=true">May 22, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Juli" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Juli" href="/user/show/38617426-juli">Juli</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audiobook 9781974901326" href="/book/show/45994519-the-secret-adversary">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/38617426-juli?shelf=backlist-read-2019">backlist-read-2019</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/38617426-juli?shelf=read-audiobooks-2019">read-audiobooks-2019</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2830538704" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17619978564521386467">Agatha Christie has been my favorite author since I was 9 and spent a summer break from school reading Hercule Poirot novels. I decided to revisit her books yet again...in publication order. The Secret Adversary, Christie's second novel, was published in 1922. It introduces Tommy & Tuppence, two characters that would go on to star in three more novels and a short story collection. The final Tommy & Tuppence novel, Postern of Fate, was the last book Agatha Christie wrote before her death, but not</span>
  <span id="freeText17619978564521386467" style="display:none">Agatha Christie has been my favorite author since I was 9 and spent a summer break from school reading Hercule Poirot novels. I decided to revisit her books yet again...in publication order. The Secret Adversary, Christie's second novel, was published in 1922. It introduces Tommy &amp; Tuppence, two characters that would go on to star in three more novels and a short story collection. The final Tommy &amp; Tuppence novel, Postern of Fate, was the last book Agatha Christie wrote before her death, but not the last one published.<br /><br />In this first story, Tommy and Tuppence are still single (they married each other later) and trying to find employment after the end of World War I. Both are running out of money and getting a bit desperate, but they don't want to tie themselves to boring, run-of-the-mill jobs following all the excitement of the war era. They decide to form a partnership, The Young Adventurers, Ltd, and advertise for unusual jobs just to keep their lives interesting. Before they even place their first advertisement, they get an offer for employment......and end up over their heads in a case of missing persons, international espionage, and murderous, sneaky villains. They yearned for excitement -- and they got it! <br /><br />I listened to the audio book version of this story (Dreamscape Media) and had the best time. The story is a bit dated after almost 100 years, but that's what made it an enjoyable listen. I had to smile each time Tuppence called someone "Old Bean.'' I loved all the 1920s lingo and social commentary about women not wanting to return to a quiet life after the war. Tommy and Tuppence are wonderful, young characters starting out in life in the years between the wars. They want excitement and security in a world that has irrevocably changed. Makes for a very enjoyable listening experience. <br /><br />The Dreamscape audio book is narrated by Emma Fenney and runs just over 8 1/2 hours. Fenney has a pleasant voice and reads at a nice pace. She does a great job voicing all the different characters. <br /><br />All in all, a fun listening experience! I am having the best time re-visiting Christie's books. She's been my favorite author for 41 years for a reason! On to her 3rd book -- Murder on the Links. Hercule Poirot! </span>
  <a data-text-id="17619978564521386467" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1670849153" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1670849153" />
    <a title="Vimal Thiagarajan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/27250071-vimal-thiagarajan"><img alt="Vimal Thiagarajan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1511490522p2/27250071.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1670849153?book_show_action=true">Jun 16, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Vimal Thiagarajan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Vimal Thiagarajan" href="/user/show/27250071-vimal-thiagarajan">Vimal Thiagarajan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780062074355" href="/book/show/11769046-the-secret-adversary">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1670849153" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9645321518819655987">Not the usual Christie mystery. This is a John Buchan style ripping yarn with light-weight espionage and a heavy emphasis on adventure.Initially I found the plot so light on logic and the situations so uncharacteristically contrived and co-incidence driven that it made me look back at the cover to confirm if I was reading a Christie or a Wodehouse. But it picked up gradually and then ended in a massive flourish. The mystery component, though not entirely unpredictable, was handled quite adeptly </span>
  <span id="freeText9645321518819655987" style="display:none">Not the usual Christie mystery. This is a John Buchan style ripping yarn with light-weight espionage and a heavy emphasis on adventure.Initially I found the plot so light on logic and the situations so uncharacteristically contrived and co-incidence driven that it made me look back at the cover to confirm if I was reading a Christie or a Wodehouse. But it picked up gradually and then ended in a massive flourish. The mystery component, though not entirely unpredictable, was handled quite adeptly as usual. But what I liked most about the book was how well fleshed out most of the characters were. Only Christie would be able to put me wise on how every other dialogue from the hustling Hersheimmer cracked me up. An extra-star just for those crafty dialogues. A cool read.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9645321518819655987" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2660193125?book_show_action=true">Jan 05, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Vikas Singh" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Vikas Singh" href="/user/show/23007922-vikas-singh">Vikas Singh</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780007111466" href="/book/show/282900.The_Secret_Adversary">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23007922-vikas-singh?shelf=owned-book">owned-book</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2660193125" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer874697185908406427">Tommy and Tuppence adventures are best enjoyed only after you have read Miss Marple and Hercule Poirot’s adventures. Only then you can marvel at the creative genius of Agatha Christie and the fun she would have had creating Tommy and Tuppence. The secret adversary is a fast paced thriller involving the world of espionage and once you have started, you just cannot put it down. Added to this is the excellent chemistry between the two amateur detectives. Thoroughly enjoyable read.</span>

          </span>

<div id="review_547883825" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/547883825" />
    <a title="C." class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10501026-c"><img alt="C." src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1578542204p2/10501026.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/547883825?book_show_action=true">Feb 27, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="C." class="user" itemprop="url" name="C." href="/user/show/10501026-c">C.</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780553240351" href="/book/show/3974474-the-secret-adversary">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10501026-c?shelf=riedel-titles-2013">riedel-titles-2013</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer547883825" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4739422720215037324"><b>Agatha Christie</b> pages impress upon you sharply; even someone sampling the queen of mystery as late as I am. I was astonished by the plot intricacy in <i>"The Mysterious Affair At Styles"</i> but had a feeling there were better stories. Immediately, second novel "<b>The Secret Adversary</b>" is a step up. I'm drawn to every stage, the settings are far more dynamic, and this time: I'm responsive to the characters. Many revere this title as the introduction to <i>Tommy & Tuppence</i> but I'm entering this experience wi</span>
  <span id="freeText4739422720215037324" style="display:none"><b>Agatha Christie</b> pages impress upon you sharply; even someone sampling the queen of mystery as late as I am. I was astonished by the plot intricacy in <i>"The Mysterious Affair At Styles"</i> but had a feeling there were better stories. Immediately, second novel "<b>The Secret Adversary</b>" is a step up. I'm drawn to every stage, the settings are far more dynamic, and this time: I'm responsive to the characters. Many revere this title as the introduction to <i>Tommy &amp; Tuppence</i> but I'm entering this experience without any knowledge of <b>Agatha</b> and have the pleasure of every discovery coming to me.<br /><br />The publication year 1922 apparently succeeds <i>World War I</i> because England speaks of tight finances and jobs. Reunited chums <i>Tommy &amp; Tuppence</i>, dare to suggest they should advertise willingness to do anything, anywhere for money. They find themselves dangerously but honourably employed by British intelligence! A covert search for an American girl named <i>Jane Finn</i> divvies into three intense directions once they are aided by her wealthy cousin <i>Julius</i>. The chapters highlight each fast-paced excursion, including a kidnapping of both lead characters; disappearing one after the other in different directions.<br /><br />What I admire about this novel in particular, goes beyond the ampleness of vibrant events to keep the pages turning with intrigue. An originality is noticeable at once, a treat for a frequent reader. We’re used to television sitcoms and movies in which a distressed protagonist avoids police, or telling anyone what's going on for fear of repercussions; when it was plainly silly not to enlist help. In this cliché, lies are woven but inevitably need to be explained and help requested after all. The frankness of all three heroes catches us off-guard and the effect of their boldness is entertaining. Accidentally accurate passwords, quick thinking, and suave language abound.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4739422720215037324" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2328400660" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2328400660" />
    <a title="Heidi" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/25243113-heidi"><img alt="Heidi" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1458594675p2/25243113.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2328400660?book_show_action=true">Apr 07, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Heidi" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Heidi" href="/user/show/25243113-heidi">Heidi</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25243113-heidi?shelf=2018">2018</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2328400660" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1965484389011390013">I’ve heard so many wonderful things about Agatha Christie’s books, but for whatever reason have never read one. When I saw that James was holding an Agatha Christie Readathon for April, I jumped on the chance to try at least a couple of her books. I am happy to say that I was pleasantly surprised with the amount of joy I had while reading The Secret Adversary. <br/><br/>One of my favorite aspects of this book was Christie’s writing style. There was something just so light and airy toward the beginning of </span>
  <span id="freeText1965484389011390013" style="display:none">I’ve heard so many wonderful things about Agatha Christie’s books, but for whatever reason have never read one. When I saw that James was holding an Agatha Christie Readathon for April, I jumped on the chance to try at least a couple of her books. I am happy to say that I was pleasantly surprised with the amount of joy I had while reading The Secret Adversary. <br /><br />One of my favorite aspects of this book was Christie’s writing style. There was something just so light and airy toward the beginning of the book. Then, when the more suspenseful parts of the book began to take over, Christie changed her tone to one that grasped my hand and quickly pulled me along for the suspenseful ride. It was a clever trick – to give the reader a false sense of security that this might be a light read, but it actually turns out to be an extremely eventful ride where I found my heart beating quickly several times throughout.<br /><br />Tommy and Tuppence’s chemistry was sweet and one that I really loved reading. I knew from the beginning what their future would hold, and yet I was still happy for them. It would have been nice, however, to have gotten to know their backgrounds better. Though perhaps how they formed their friendship wasn’t what Christie was trying to portray.<br /><br />As far as the mystery aspect of the story is concerned, I would say that I was partially right in solving it toward the end. I had my suspicions right from the beginning, but kept flip flopping between two potential “bad” guys. For this, I commend Christie’s ability to keep me guessing until the end.<br /><br />There are several questions left for the readers to think about toward the end. Without giving too much away, some I have are – what happened to some people in the story? What was in the document that everyone wanted? Will we see the same characters in the subsequent books in the Tommy &amp; Tuppence series?<br /><br />Overall, this was a book that I enjoyed very much so and finally understand the love that people have for this author. Though I would have liked a bit more character development and to have known the answers to some of my questions, in general, I will definitely be checking out her other works! I highly recommend this to anyone who enjoys a good mystery!<br /><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://bookloverblogs.com/2018/04/07/book-review-the-secret-adversary-by-agatha-christie/">https://bookloverblogs.com/2018/04/07...</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="1965484389011390013" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1045176842" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1045176842" />
    <a title="Richard Derus" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3920693-richard-derus"><img alt="Richard Derus" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1494992210p2/3920693.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1045176842?book_show_action=true">Sep 04, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Richard Derus" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Richard Derus" href="/user/show/3920693-richard-derus">Richard Derus</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/18073088-the-secret-adversary">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1045176842" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13589745054170965883">Rating: 3* of five for both book and movie<br/><br/><b>The Publisher Says</b>: After WW1, childhood pals Tommy Beresford and "Tuppence" Prudence Cowley, lack money and prospects, become adventurers for the British Government. Rich American Julius P. Hersheimmer, powerful Mr Whittington, and an evil mastermind's conspiracy all seek Jane Finn, given papers vital to peace by an agent at the sinking of the Luisitania. Kidnaps, escapes.<br/><br/><b>My Review</b>: The novel is a dated piece, lots of hoopla about Bolsheviks and the Gen</span>
  <span id="freeText13589745054170965883" style="display:none">Rating: 3* of five for both book and movie<br><br><b>The Publisher Says</b>: After WW1, childhood pals Tommy Beresford and "Tuppence" Prudence Cowley, lack money and prospects, become adventurers for the British Government. Rich American Julius P. Hersheimmer, powerful Mr Whittington, and an evil mastermind's conspiracy all seek Jane Finn, given papers vital to peace by an agent at the sinking of the Luisitania. Kidnaps, escapes.<br><br><b>My Review</b>: The novel is a dated piece, lots of hoopla about Bolsheviks and the General Strike and Socialism!! Socialism!! Tuppence is a right little minx. Tommy is a public school boy in the most English sense of those words. It was, I suppose, delicious in 1922 for a mere woman to be the instigator of an adventurous life for the borning couple on the other side of the law; that she doesn't have to Pay Dearly For It is truly eyebrow-raising.<br><br>Sixty years later, along comes Francesca Annis to embody Tuppence, and speak the faithfully adapted words Dame Agatha wrote. Annis is just lovely. She does a marvelous job of scheming behind a melting smile. But all the to-ing and fro-ing! Just-missed-'em and who-said-what moments galore. It creaks, in other words, to more savvy modern ears, very much the way Mary Roberts Rinehart's books do, or Georgette Heyer's mysteries do.<br><br>All that said, however, I didn't hurl the book aside or stop the film. Because in the end, it was fun. Just a bit silly, but still fun, and to me that's worth a lot. But the Big Reveal is just so durned obvious! And the American character so, so buffoonish! Oh well, autres temps autres moeurs. It doesn't do to apply too much modern sensibility to olden days. But I will say this to modern audiences: Either medium, go in expecting a relaxed pace (the film is 2 hours!) and you'll be better off by the end. <br><br>The chase scene with a 1915 Rolls-Royce amazed me.<br><br><a href="http://creativecommons.org/licenses/by-nc-sa/3.0/deed.en_US" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img alt="Creative Commons License" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380148217i/680962.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br>This work is licensed under a <a href="http://creativecommons.org/licenses/by-nc-sa/3.0/deed.en_US" rel="nofollow noopener">Creative Commons Attribution-NonCommercial-ShareAlike 3.0 Unported License</a>.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13589745054170965883" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer636972116" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4940284558544977221"> *SPOILERS* Let me get this out of the way - I think Mr Brown should have been Julius and not Sir James. The writer, bless her, should not have tried for a last twist in the tale and should have stuck to Julius as the villain. I don't like it much when the super villain as in here, is revealed to be an unimportant character on whom the spotlight is never shined for an adequate time. <br/><br/> However I gave this book four stars because despite its faults it delivers a quality pacing rhythm. It's a shame </span>
  <span id="freeText4940284558544977221" style="display:none"> *SPOILERS* Let me get this out of the way - I think Mr Brown should have been Julius and not Sir James. The writer, bless her, should not have tried for a last twist in the tale and should have stuck to Julius as the villain. I don't like it much when the super villain as in here, is revealed to be an unimportant character on whom the spotlight is never shined for an adequate time. <br /><br /> However I gave this book four stars because despite its faults it delivers a quality pacing rhythm. It's a shame Agatha Christie neglected her less popular characters, instead being bent on milking Poirot dry. These adventuresome spy novels of hers are a delight to read. I had no problem with Tommy and Tuppence, they were fine too. I remember quite a few Christie novels to which I gave 5 stars and they weren't perfect, so I'm sticking to my guns.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4940284558544977221" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2342505764" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2342505764" />
    <a title="Christine PNW" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5664767-christine-pnw"><img alt="Christine PNW" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1449339788p2/5664767.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2342505764?book_show_action=true">Apr 03, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Christine PNW" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Christine PNW" href="/user/show/5664767-christine-pnw">Christine PNW</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/6114737-the-secret-adversary">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2342505764" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14538214754015202618">Published in 1922, <i>The Secret Adversary</i> was Christie’s second novel, coming directly on the heels of <i>The Mysterious Affair At Styles</i>, her first Poirot outing which was published in 1920. For the first decade or so of Christie’s career she dabbled heavily in the thriller/espionage genre, publishing <i>The Man in the Brown Suit, The Secret of Chimneys, The Seven Dials Mystery and The Big Four</i>, all of which deal with international crime gangs and conspiracies with varying levels of competence and succ</span>
  <span id="freeText14538214754015202618" style="display:none">Published in 1922, <i>The Secret Adversary</i> was Christie’s second novel, coming directly on the heels of <i>The Mysterious Affair At Styles</i>, her first Poirot outing which was published in 1920. For the first decade or so of Christie’s career she dabbled heavily in the thriller/espionage genre, publishing <i>The Man in the Brown Suit, The Secret of Chimneys, The Seven Dials Mystery and The Big Four</i>, all of which deal with international crime gangs and conspiracies with varying levels of competence and success. After the 1929 publication of <i>The Big Four</i> (which is nominally a Poirot, the plot of which, however, deals less with garden variety murder than with a strange, Austin Powers-esque international crime conspiracy), her publisher must have convinced her to abandon her not wholly convincing thriller career in favor of writing whodunnits, because she doesn’t write another international spy thriller until the second Tommy and Tuppence novel was published in 1941.<br /><br />I am of mixed emotions about this because I find her early thrillers (with the exception of <i>The Big Four</i>, which was absolutely terrible) to be weirdly charming in their innocence about the incompetence of the political criminal/international criminal mastermind. <i>The Secret Adversary </i>definitely falls into the category of charming and innocent. The basic plot is whisper thin (literally – it’s based on Tommy overhearing two people whispering about a woman named Jane Finn) and is generally about the possession of some government documents by a young woman (with amnesia. Yes, really) and an international crime syndicate who want to get a hold of those documents in order to foment revolution in England. If this doesn’t make any sense to you, that’s because it doesn’t actually make any sense. Tommy and Tuppence are two broke Bright Young Things who decide that the best way for them to come into possession of a few pounds is to place an ad in the newspaper, to try to hire themselves out as adventurers.<br /><br />It’s preposterous and in the real world (or in modern fiction, which goes for verisimilitude) they’d have been dead within about 25 pages, and the rest of the book would’ve been spent with the professionals attempting to figure out why these two charming young people ended up murdered by terrorists. That’s not how this one goes, though. It feels like such an innocent world in <i>The Secret Adversary</i> (and in <i>The Secret of Chimneys</i> as well). I can only wonder if this was simply a reaction to the trauma that WWI inflicted on the British people, and surmise that, perhaps, what they really needed was to believe that a pair of children, with very little money, a great deal of sparkling wit and a fetching hat could, in fact, save the world. Because there is nothing even remotely convincing or realistic about this plot, but somehow, it’s impossible to care because it is all so delightful.<br /><br />This was my first time reading <i>The Secret Adversary</i>, and I doubt that it will become one of my favorites although I thoroughly enjoyed it. I went into it convinced that Tommy and Tuppence were lifted wholesale from Dashiell Hammett’s Nick and Nora Charles – imagine my surprise when I actually looked it up and learned that T &amp; T predated N &amp; N by a dozen years. I should’ve known better, though – The Queen sets trends, she doesn’t follow them.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14538214754015202618" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
